B006UG90RM|3.0|I feel fortunate in that I am a fan of both Van Halen's. I realize that there was a third incarnation, but I consider that to be a scientific experiment gone horribly wrong. I fondly remember when I was a little kid going over to my friend's house and listening to his older brother's vinyl copy of 1984. I absolutely loved it. They also had cable so I saw the videos for Jump, Panama, and Hot For Teacher on MTV. Those memories are indelible. On the other hand, it wasn't until I was a teenager in 92 when I really got into music. The first VH album I actually purchased was For Unlawful Carnal Knowledge. Again, I absolutely loved it. At that tender young age, I was blown away by the musicianship and Sammy's \\"high octane\\" voice as it was described in an article I read way back when. I then went on to acquire 5150 and OU812, which I also thought were outstanding. Being a naive young kid, I was completely unaware of this Sammy vs DLR debate. Back then, there was no internet so you just liked what you liked; it was a better time really. So now we fast forward to my college days. I took a shuttle bus to campus and the bus driver was playing all this old VH stuff from the DLR era; again blown away. I thought to myself that I must acquire this amazing music. The first DLR era album I acquired was Women and Children First. Having grown accustomed to the Sammy Hagar fronted Van Halen, it took me a while to warm up to the DLR albums, but I soon embraced them as great works in their own right. I was especially impressed when I finally purchased the first two DLR albums; I don't think I need to elaborate. When I acquired 1984, all those great memories came back of my first introduction to the mighty Van Halen. So now, here we are in the present. I give this album 3 stars because of the engineering. I read a few reviews regarding \\"dynamic compression\\" and I must agree with those critiques. The songs on A Different Kind of Truth are amazing, but the engineering is awful. I am old fashioned so I am listening to this album on my stereo and it is just a wall of noise; so disappointing. I can tell that there is some amazing music going on, especially with Eddie's guitar playing. Unfortunately, the great VH sound is lost in the production of ADKOT. Still, a Van Halen album after almost 14 years of waiting is a welcome addition to their legacy. Maybe if I convert the album to MP3 it will sound better. I do miss the backing vocals of Michael Anthony. No disrespect to Wolfgang, but I don't think I'm alone in wishing that the oringinal Van Halen lineup was back together; all four members. Isn't this what we've all longed for? But again, I'm kind of glad I joined the party late because I respect Van Halen's full body of work, both with Sammy and DLR. There's even a few songs I like from Van Halen III. Without You is a great VH song regardless of who is on vocals. I'm just so sick of this ridiculous competition between DLR and Sammy. The two Chickenfoot albums are really great. And aside from the production, the new VH is great too! Eddie and Alex are constants on all of the VH recordings and both of these gentlemen are outstanding musicians. It doesn't really matter to me who is on vocals; the Van Halen brothers will always deliver. I hope there is more great music to come from these guys.

0312576463|3.0|SPOILER ALERT.  IF YOU HAVE NOT READ THIS BOOK, YOU MAY WANT TO SKIP THE LAST PARAGRAPH OF THIS REVIEW.<br /><br />A long time ago, when I was reading everything I could about the Ancient Egyptians, I read somewhere that they had invented graph paper so that they could ensure that their wall art and engineering works were as precise as possible (bear with me).  According to my source, they were positively obsessed with having everything be in its proper proportions.  And that's the feeling I got when I read \\"Freedom\\".  I felt like Mr. Franzen had plotted each and every character on his or her own piece of graph paper, leading to a very precise enumeration of said character, but one in which the character did not have any room to breathe.  And I also felt that he had done the same thing with the story.  And, yes, as other reviewers have said (especially the ones giving the book 1 star), there are a lot of improbable elements in the book, giving it a \\"John Irvingish\\" tinge, but that still does not mean, as far as I am concerned, that there is anything truly spontaneous in this book.  Now, don't get me wrong.  I am very, very partial to \\"world building\\" science fiction books, and books with lots of back story,  and you can dump your info-dumps on me any time, but I still like to read a book that seems to be alive and breathing.  I kept reading because all the detail was fascinating to me, so much so in fact that I felt like a sort of voyeur.  That's when I didn't feel like I was reading the writing of a professional gossip.  I kept on reading even though the book felt as stiff and lifeless as one of those Egyptian tomb paintings, because I wanted to see what weird thing was coming up around the next bend - I guess for the same reason that people rubberneck a roadside accident scene.  I kept reading even though I really did not care about any of the characters and what was going to happen to them.  In the end, even with all the details of the plot and of the main character's personal lives, I was left knowing very little about why any of them did the things they wound up doing. In short, I think the book is well-written on a technical level, but does not really hang together as a novel.  There is just a total lack of feeling there.<br /><br />SPOILER ALERT<br /><br />P.S. I could not feel any liking or empathy for any of the main characters, all of whom, with the exception of Richard and Lalitha, basically seemed to be dishonest and/or dislikeable in so may different ways.  I liked Richard because \\"what you saw was what you got\\" - there was no real hypocrisy there.  I did not know what to make of Lalitha - I did not get a good feel from the author about what motivated her, but I also that that \\"what you saw was what you got\\".  Connie was a cipher - I don't know what Joey saw in her, and the author does not communicate this.

0385344228|4.0|As a former criminal prosecutor and as a trial lawyer defending major civil cases, I can speak to the accuracy of Defending Jacob's trial sequences, the center of this entertaining and well-written novel.  Landay conveys properly the truth that everything that happens in a courtroom is evidence, including the non-verbal behavior of each participant and each spectator.  As a parent and spouse, I can say that the complex relationships depicted in Defending Jacob sound authentic.  Without giving away too much of the novel -- and I haven't read the other 100+ reviews, so if anyone ever reads this review, he or she might know everything I'm trying to protect anyway -- I will offer a few minor criticisms: (a) the testimony of the main police witness against Jacob is virtually all hearsay and objectionable, yet Jacob's attorney never objects; (b) what are intended to be surprises -- the twists of plot -- do not surprise (at least they didn't surprise me) except for the very ending.  As I think about comparisons to the work of Scott Turow, I can say I enjoy Turow's writing more, but that's like saying an A+ is better than an A.  So, with all that, I highly recommend Defending Jacob.[[ASIN:B006WEHL6E Community and Other Stories (Nate & Adel and Other Stories)]][[ASIN:B005KB98R0 Nate and Adel and Other Stories]]
